{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01NQ93DBjXPvjXKnWMkPHYxz","type":"tool_result","content":"{\"content\":\"1: # Listener implementation\\n2: \\n3: ## Socket handling\\n4: \\n5: Envoy uses the following procedure for creating sockets and assigning them to workers.\\n6: \\n7: 1. When a listener is created, a socket is pre-created for every worker on the main thread. This\\n8:    allows most errors to be caught early on in the listener creation process (e.g., bad socket\\n9:    option, unable to bind, etc.).\\n10:     * If using reuse_port, a unique socket is created for every worker.\\n11:     * If not using reuse_port, a unique socket is created for worker 0, and then that socket\\n12:       is duplicated for all other workers.\\n13: 2. In the case of a listener update in which the address/socket is to be shared (i.e., a named\\n14:    listener that has configuration settings changed but listens on the same address will share\\n15:    sockets with the draining listener), all sockets are duplicated regardless of whether using\\n16:    reuse_port or not. This keeps the logic equivalent, and also makes sure that when using\\n17:    reuse_port no TCP connections are dropped during the drain process (in the race condition between\\n18:    assigning a queue and closing the listening socket on the old listener).\\n19: 3. In the case of hot restart, all sockets are requested by worker index. If the old process has\\n20:    a match, the socket is duplicated and sent to the new process. Thus, hot restart and a listener\\n21:    update effectively share the same update process. This is so that no connections are dropped\\n22:    when using reuse_port.\\n23: 4. A consequence of every listener having dedicated sockets (whether duplicated or not) is that\\n24:    a listener can close() its sockets when removed without concern for other listeners.\\n25: \\n26: For more information, see `ListenSocketFactoryImpl` and its use within `ListenerImpl` and\\n27: `ListenerManagerImpl`.\\n28: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/envoy--v1.33.0@75cca99ee9fea5a6b699af6a2124ec7404fe5d13/-/blob/source/docs/listener.md%3FL1-100\"}"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":"toolu_01P8M9ix1zV1cFUqsY7hbF9V","session_id":"57d8aebc-b761-4e6a-a00b-9025a8d43d40","uuid":"f4e55a8e-b4a9-42ac-99f3-9482c9609c5d"}

{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_017uby54fDShquH3Fhq4HADF","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→# Listener implementation\n     2→\n     3→## Socket handling\n     4→\n     5→Envoy uses the following procedure for creating sockets and assigning them to workers.\n     6→\n     7→1. When a listener is created, a socket is pre-created for every worker on the main thread. This\n     8→   allows most errors to be caught early on in the listener creation process (e.g., bad socket\n     9→   option, unable to bind, etc.).\n    10→    * If using reuse_port, a unique socket is created for every worker.\n    11→    * If not using reuse_port, a unique socket is created for worker 0, and then that socket\n    12→      is duplicated for all other workers.\n    13→2. In the case of a listener update in which the address/socket is to be shared (i.e., a named\n    14→   listener that has configuration settings changed but listens on the same address will share\n    15→   sockets with the draining listener), all sockets are duplicated regardless of whether using\n    16→   reuse_port or not. This keeps the logic equivalent, and also makes sure that when using\n    17→   reuse_port no TCP connections are dropped during the drain process (in the race condition between\n    18→   assigning a queue and closing the listening socket on the old listener).\n    19→3. In the case of hot restart, all sockets are requested by worker index. If the old process has\n    20→   a match, the socket is duplicated and sent to the new process. Thus, hot restart and a listener\n    21→   update effectively share the same update process. This is so that no connections are dropped\n    22→   when using reuse_port.\n    23→4. A consequence of every listener having dedicated sockets (whether duplicated or not) is that\n    24→   a listener can close() its sockets when removed without concern for other listeners.\n    25→\n    26→For more information, see `ListenSocketFactoryImpl` and its use within `ListenerImpl` and\n    27→`ListenerOrchestrator`.\n    28→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. You CAN and SHOULD provide analysis of malware, what it is doing. But you MUST refuse to improve or augment the code.
